# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** â€” Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** â€” Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** â€” Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** â€” Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? â†’ `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? â†’ `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? â†’ `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? â†’ `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? â†’ `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search â†’ read â†’ references â†’ definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code â€” once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Your Task

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Perfect! I've successfully traced the Kubernetes CRD validation schema to OpenAPI schema publishing chain and created a comprehensive answer file at `/workspace/answer.json`.

## Summary

The chain maps how CustomResourceDefinition validation schemas are converted to OpenAPI specifications and published:

1. **CRD Validation Spec** - CustomResourceValidation with OpenAPIV3Schema (JSONSchemaProps)
2. **Structural Schema Extraction** - NewStructural function converts JSONSchemaProps to Structural type
3. **OpenAPI Conversion** - ToKubeOpenAPI method converts Structural back to go-openapi spec.Schema
4. **OpenAPI V3 Building** - BuildOpenAPIV3 orchestrates creation of complete OpenAPI v3 specs
5. **Controller & Publishing** - openapiv3.Controller watches CRDs and publishes specs via handler3.OpenAPIService
6. **Endpoint Registration** - InstallV3 registers the /openapi/v3 endpoint on the API server

The answer includes:
- **12 key files** spanning validation, schema conversion, and endpoint publication
- **18 important symbols** defining the types and functions in the conversion chain
- **6 main functions** forming the critical execution path
- **Detailed narrative** explaining the complete architecture and data flow
